              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer345247771">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14968050114858720288">Don't mind me, just crying my eyes out. <br /><br />This was WAY better than I remember it being, and I remember it being pretty darn good. J.K. Rowling is a writing goddess and I can't believe how much foresight and planning went into this series. She already hints at the horcruxes and many other things in this book that don't show up until much later. Definitely one of my favorites in the series! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_68913564">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68913564" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" alt="Stephen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/68913564?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 01, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="user" title="Stephen">Stephen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Paperback 9780439139601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-hugo" class="actionLinkLite">award-nominee-hugo</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-locus" class="actionLinkLite">award-nominee-locus</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=multiple-award-nominee" class="actionLinkLite">multiple-award-nominee</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-winner-hugo" class="actionLinkLite">award-winner-hugo</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-bram-stoker" class="actionLinkLite">award-nominee-bram-stoker</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=potteresque" class="actionLinkLite">potteresque</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2000-2005" class="actionLinkLite">2000-2005</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=comfort-food" class="actionLinkLite">comfort-food</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer68913564">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7518100950352228981">This was the beginning of my addiction to <strong>POT</strong>ter. I had previously <em>experimented</em> with and enjoyed <strong>POT</strong>ter on 3 different occasions, but could easily have walked away and never touched the stuff again. Then, under some pressure from some <strong>POT</strong>ter<strong>HEAD</strong> peers of mine, I tried the newest blend called <strong>the Goblet</strong>...and everything changed. As the warm, easy, potato chip prose crossed my blood-brain barrier, euphoria ensued. My inner child was smitten. <br /><br />I...was...hooked and I...was...happy. <br /><br />Ignore the so-call</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7518100950352228981">This was the beginning of my addiction to <strong>POT</strong>ter. I had previously <em>experimented</em> with and enjoyed <strong>POT</strong>ter on 3 different occasions, but could easily have walked away and never touched the stuff again. Then, under some pressure from some <strong>POT</strong>ter<strong>HEAD</strong> peers of mine, I tried the newest blend called <strong>the Goblet</strong>...and everything changed. As the warm, easy, potato chip prose crossed my blood-brain barrier, euphoria ensued. My inner child was smitten. <br /><br />I...was...hooked and I...was...happy. <br /><br />Ignore the so-called "experts" who say <strong>POT</strong>ter is brain cell killing pap. Don’t listen to those jaded, book snobby squares. Most of them are wound so tight they wouldn’t know a good book if it sat on their face and wriggled. <br /><br /><strong>POT</strong>ter makes you feel good. <strong>POT</strong>ter makes you smile. <strong>POT</strong>ter makes you joyous and giggly. Hell, <strong>POT</strong>ter makes you want to use the word giggly. <br /><br /><strong>POT</strong>ter is enjoyable and fun. That's enough for me. <br /><br />So what made <strong> the Goblet</strong> so much more addicting than the rest of the <strong>POT</strong>ter I had tried. Part of it was that I had already seen the movies (up through Order of the Phoenix) before I got my hands on genuine <strong>POT</strong>ter. The first 3 were fun but I felt like I had already "been there done that" as they were pretty faithfully adaptated for the screen. Still enjoyable, but not enough to put the <strong>POT</strong>ter monkey on my back. <br /><br />Then came <strong>the Goblet</strong> of <strong>POT</strong>ter and it was a big, huge, tightly-rolled fatty at 750 pages. The cut, diluted movie strain couldn’t hope to be as potent as the primo original and the story was finally given the room to breathe and take on an epic feel. It was completely addictive. The world-building details started coming fast and furious and the characters were given considerably increased depth. Add that to Rowling’s breezy, “ear friendly” prose and I found myself spaced out for hours turning the pages and still hungering for more. <br /><br />It’s high praise indeed when I say that 750 pages did not contain a single dull, ploddy moment. This was fun and wonderful and a pleasure to experience. It deserves to be recognized for the iconic work that it is in the realm of YA fantasy. <br /><br />Is it popcorn? Certainly. <br />Is it a joy to read? Definitely. <br />Is it one I HIGHLY RECOMMEND to all lovers of feel good, comfort food? YES. <br /><br />5.0 stars. <br /><br />Winner: Hugo Award for Best Science Fiction Novel (2001) <br />Nominee: Locus Award for Best Fantasy Novel (2001) <br />Nominee: Bram Stoker Award (YA) for Best Novel (2001)<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7518100950352228981">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/864890.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Paperback 9780747550990" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3452652-raeleen-lemay?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3452652-raeleen-lemay?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer108852901">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9887534310362407424"><em> Re-Read in December 2014 for Harry Christmas To You </em><br /><br />SO I HAVE A FEW NOTES ON THIS ONE:<br /><br />-at the beginning, Voldemort says to Wormtail, "I will allow you to perform an essential task for me, one that many of my followers would give their right hands to perform..." OMG J.K. ROWLING FORESHADOWS EVERYTHINGGGG<br /><br />-when the Weasley men come to Privet Drive through the Dursleys' fireplace is just.... priceless. Yet ANOTHER scene that I wish had made it into the movie.<br /><br />-We get to meet Bill in this book (way e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9887534310362407424"><em> Re-Read in December 2014 for Harry Christmas To You </em><br /><br />SO I HAVE A FEW NOTES ON THIS ONE:<br /><br />-at the beginning, Voldemort says to Wormtail, "I will allow you to perform an essential task for me, one that many of my followers would give their right hands to perform..." OMG J.K. ROWLING FORESHADOWS EVERYTHINGGGG<br /><br />-when the Weasley men come to Privet Drive through the Dursleys' fireplace is just.... priceless. Yet ANOTHER scene that I wish had made it into the movie.<br /><br />-We get to meet Bill in this book (way earlier than in the movies, I might add), and Mrs. Weasley is very disapproving of how Bill looks. I love that Bill stood up for himself and was like NOBODY GIVE AN F HOW I LOOK, AND NEITHER DO IIIIII. It was a nice thing to throw in there.<br /><br />-Dobby is also in this book more, and seeing how different he is was really fun.<br /><br />-Harry and Ron fighting made my heart hurt so much.<br /><br />-All of the drama at the Yule Ball just made me SQUEEE because it's so obvious that Ron and Hermione like each other and they just don't want to admit it and GAH. THE FEELS.<br /><br />-I also love how much Hermione stands up for what she believes in, which you can particularly see in this book. She wants justice for the house-elves, she won't let Ron get away with being an idiot (like when he says he just wants a pretty girl to go to the ball with), and she is especially confident in this book as well. Malfoy and many other people are constantly teasing her, but she is completely above it, and for that I admire her.<br /><br />-WHEN HARRY IS LISTENING TO HAGRID AND MADAME MAXIME AND HE SEES THE BEETLE? IMAGINE IF HE HAD JUST STEPPED ON IT? WOULDN'T THAT HAVE BEEN GREAT?<br /><br />-I completely forgot about the part where Harry sees Barty Crouch on the Marauders Map! He was so close to finding out something big, but then things got crazy and he didn't, but WHOA. SO CLOSE. <br /><br />-Cedric's death hit me a lot harder than it ever has before... He was such an amazing person, and I wish that he could have survived so him and Harry could have been buddies.<br /><br />-VOLDEMORT FORESHADOWS HORCRUXES IN THIS BOOK. TWO MORE BOOKS UNTIL HARRY ACTUALLY LEARNS THOUGH.<br /><br /><br />ok so I think it's safe to say that this is one of my favorites in the series for sure. Probably in the top 3. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1423283686">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5945704361026294298">I'm apparently the crankiest person on earth, because this was my least favorite Potter book yet. (AZKABAN being my favorite!) It's mostly because:<br /><br />1. There is too much tournamenting for my taste. <br />2. I hate the house elves. :O<br />3. The word "quietly" is egregiously overused. It loses its effectiveness because it appears so often.<br />4. There are moments when Harry and Ron behave like stereotypical stupid boys (I know, I know, they're 14...doesn't mean I can't be annoyed with them.)<br /><br />The book gets an extra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5945704361026294298">I'm apparently the crankiest person on earth, because this was my least favorite Potter book yet. (AZKABAN being my favorite!) It's mostly because:<br /><br />1. There is too much tournamenting for my taste. <br />2. I hate the house elves. :O<br />3. The word "quietly" is egregiously overused. It loses its effectiveness because it appears so often.<br />4. There are moments when Harry and Ron behave like stereotypical stupid boys (I know, I know, they're 14...doesn't mean I can't be annoyed with them.)<br /><br />The book gets an extra star because the last 10 chapters were very good, though, and I loved:<br /><br />1. that Hermione gets a makeover, but then matter-of-factly says it's too much trouble to straighten her hair every day.<br />2. the creepy thing in the blanket <br />3. Cedric! Poor brave boy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[WHY DID NO ONE TELL ME. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_5475722">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5475722" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/332008-susan" class="left imgcol" title="Susan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1188658740p2/332008.jpg" alt="Susan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/5475722?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 04, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/332008-susan" class="user" title="Susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Paperback 9780439139601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5475722">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4831545375873046265">Now THAT'S a book! The groove that J.K. Rowling starts to find in HP 3 is fully realized in 4. Partly it's that the kids (and therefore the readers) are getting older so she can delve into more adult, complex themes and situations, and partly it's that I think she's really finding her voice. We finally got our very own HP's, I am happy to report, and it's so funny to look at them all side by side b/c of the HUGE leap in size between 3 and 4. Then they get a little tricky b/c while 4 and 5 look t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4831545375873046265">Now THAT'S a book! The groove that J.K. Rowling starts to find in HP 3 is fully realized in 4. Partly it's that the kids (and therefore the readers) are getting older so she can delve into more adult, complex themes and situations, and partly it's that I think she's really finding her voice. We finally got our very own HP's, I am happy to report, and it's so funny to look at them all side by side b/c of the HUGE leap in size between 3 and 4. Then they get a little tricky b/c while 4 and 5 look to be about the same length, the font in Order of the Phoenix is much smaller, hence a longer book. I just started that one and it honestly feels longer already. More of a book book and less of a fun afternoon's diversion. But I like these books as they get both darker and longer.<br /><br />But to focus on Goblet of Fire specifically for a moment...again, not that I think I can bring anything new to the table in discussing these books. Nevertheless, I'll throw a few ideas out there just for your reading pleasure. One thing that struck me, as I mentioned before, was the increasing maturity and complexity of situations and themes. Clearly having someone die is a huge deal and I found that whole series of events really moving this time around. I may have last time as well, but I don't remember. In a way, though, some of the more complex issues feel jarring next to the goofy concepts she originally created. Calling non-magical people "Muggles," for instance. It's just a stupid word and yes, it sounds funny and makes kids laugh, but sometimes it's hard to take all these people seriously. "Mud-bloods" on the other hand is vicious and definitely drives the point home. I just wonder if she was to do it over again if some of those terms or ideas would change a bit. Yes, we'd all like to revisit what we did/wrote when we were less sure of ourselves and our voices and ideas, but of course we can't and neither can she. And what do I know? She claims she always knew what would happen to Harry, so maybe for her "Muggle" is the ideal word.<br /><br />Since, as usual, I find it impossible to discuss the books without referencing the films, let me just say that although I hated Dobby in the movie (2?) and was glad to see him mostly cut from subsequent screen incarnations, I really loved him in this one. The dialogue is actually quite funny and Hermione's whole S.P.E.W. thing just cracks me up. Yes, I know a lot of people hate it and find it annoying and whatever, but I love it. Of course she would have a cause like that. That's who she is! And poor Winky. They're weird creatures (and OH how I love Kreacher in the next one!) and I can't decide whether I am with Hermione or everyone else on their "plight." Either way, I like that they exist; they provide a bit of moral ambiguity in a world that is mostly cleanly divided between good and evil. You might wonder about people, but for the most part they end up squarely one or the other. Other than Snape - another great piece of moral ambiguity whose complexity grows from book to book.<br /><br />I also continue to marvel at Rowling's ability to write about the teenage mind. Ron and Harry's fight is spot on, as are Hermione's various reactions to it. And oh these poor boys having to ask the girls to the feast. I wish I had known when I was in middle school how truly hard it was for boys to talk to girls like that. Although I probably wouldn't have cared, being the good self-involved teenger that I was. <br /><br />I still want to go to Hogwarts.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4831545375873046265">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_128162676">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128162676" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4324634-katya" class="left imgcol" title="Katya"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1285183076p2/4324634.jpg" alt="Katya" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/128162676?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4324634-katya" class="user" title="Katya">Katya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7339102" title="Hardcover 9789544466213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=horrible-best-friends" class="actionLinkLite">horrible-best-friends</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=teen-lit" class="actionLinkLite">teen-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=2011" class="actionLinkLite">2011</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=middle-grade" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=oh-come-on" class="actionLinkLite">oh-come-on</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=kudos-for-the-worldbuilding" class="actionLinkLite">kudos-for-the-worldbuilding</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=for-nostalgia-s-sake" class="actionLinkLite">for-nostalgia-s-sake</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=the-harry-potter-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">the-harry-potter-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer128162676">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2280237500515167115"><strong> Here be warned: This review contains cursing. </strong><br /><br />Greetings, loved ones, and let us talk of a young witch named Hermione Granger.<br /><br />Hermione is, and always has been, a delight to read. Not necessarily because she's a girl, but because she is the only character amongst those 14 year olds who actually has a good head on her shoulders. <br /><br />When I was young and gullible, I hated this book. Hated how it killed off Cedric and how bloody the series got afterwards. I hated it enough to renounce the franchize. Now</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2280237500515167115"><strong> Here be warned: This review contains cursing. </strong><br /><br />Greetings, loved ones, and let us talk of a young witch named Hermione Granger.<br /><br />Hermione is, and always has been, a delight to read. Not necessarily because she's a girl, but because she is the only character amongst those 14 year olds who actually has a good head on her shoulders. <br /><br />When I was young and gullible, I hated this book. Hated how it killed off Cedric and how bloody the series got afterwards. I hated it enough to renounce the franchize. Now that I re-read it, I still hate it, but for all different reasons. Cedric, on second reading, is as dull as toast (so I guess the movie casting must have been really spot-on). Harry has finally started to shed his unnatural maturity, and has turned just as obnoxious as most boys at 13. Ron is a wanker. So it's beyond me why Hermione hasn't stolen the spotlight here, as she is easily the most relatable character of them all.<br /><br />Let's look at her character - she is from a muggle family, but through hard work she has become the best student in the school. She studies hard, follows the rules, but makes exceptions when the circumstances are right. She comes off as stuck-up at first, but looks after her friends. She keeps her promises, even though she barely has time to take care of herself. And yet Ron is Harry's best friend, not her.<br /><br />Why?<br /><br />Harry and Ron are much closer than Harry and Hermione. In the previous book, Hermione was at odds with the boys not one, but twice, and that put a serious hinge on their friendship. Even so, that doesn't nearly come close to the drama that follows Harry and Ron's falling out in this book. And then, when they do make up, Hermione is once again pushed back as a tercery best friend, even though she sacrificed her efforts and sleep in order to help Harry learn a spell that would save his skinny ass.<br /><br />Hermione is defined by her intelligence. It falls squarely on her shoulders to help the guys when they're in a pickle - whenever they discover that rushing at an obstackle headfirst isn't going to cut it, they turn to her for advice, and she's also acutely aware of issues of inequality. In this book, she actually starts an organisation to help house elves! She stands up for Hagrid when Rita Skeeter takes a sling at him, and she kept Lupin's secret for months in book three simply because she believed he was a good guy! And where do her efforts to promote equality lead to? They're used for comedic relief.<br /><br />It's equally disgusting how little the boys seem to appreciate her. Not only do they refuse to take her seriously, they consider she's for granted. I mean, sure, Harry has lived with his relatives as an upper middle class brat (a much abused middle class brat), but Hermione's parents are dentists and yet she has a better awareness of social issues than he does! Is Rowling trying to suggest that young activism is only for women, because only women seem aware of these issues?<br /><br />But that's not even the worst this book gets. On the Yule Ball, Harry and Ron take ages before they realize Hermione is a girl, and thus, qualified to be a dance partner (obiously, they can't go with each other, altough it would be most logical, what with all the sparks flying among them). Hermione, though, refuses to be taken for granted. She knows she deserves better than to be a go-to girl, and she does - she gets to be Viktor Krum's date, and she damn well got someone who appreciates her! But are her friends happy for her? No, they're shocked, and in Ron's case, offended, that she dared *gasp* make plans without them! Ron goes as far as to make a scene - in which he (not for the first time) makes Hermione cry. This was supposed to establish some beginnings of the love between Hermione and Ron, but, quite frankly, it just makes Ron look like a wanker. <br /><br />After Rita Skeeter's article, Hermione becomes the target for bullying which, in some cases, turns rather dangerous. Grown-up witches send her hate mail packed with all sorts of deadly stuff, one of which makes the skin of her hands fall off. Ron's commentary? She should have seen it coming, messing around with the paparazzi like that. I bet the bumrag was happy she got punished for liking Krum. But that's not even what's most disturbing about this thing - it's that witches who have never even met Hermione before are willing to take Skeeter's word for it, even if the woman's as trustworthy as a snake. Even Mrs. Weasley, whose own husband got blackened twice in "The Daily Prophet", believes her! Nice message for female solidarity, Ms Rowling, real subtle.<br /><br />Again, I ask, why can't Hermione be the hero of these series? I don't think I'm alone in thinking it could be so much <a rel="nofollow" href="http://globalcomment.com/2011/in-praise-of-hermione-granger-series/">better</a>. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2280237500515167115">...more</a>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1245740844" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/29931457-franco-santos" class="left imgcol" title="Franco  Santos"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1426036813p2/29931457.jpg" alt="Franco  Santos" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1245740844?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/29931457-franco-santos" class="user" title="Franco  Santos">Franco  Santos</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/101558.Harry_Potter_y_el_C_liz_de_Fuego" title="Paperback 9788478886647" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/29931457-franco-santos?shelf=libros-en-digital" class="actionLinkLite">libros-en-digital</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1245740844">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17081000206790526141"><strong>Excelencia pura</strong>. Me encantó. En este se desarrolla una prosa más madura y oscura. No puedo decir nada más; mi amor por este libro es inefable.<blockquote> <img width="280" height="210" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428265064i/14397638._SX540_.jpg" /> </blockquote><em> —Saludémonos con una inclinación, Harry —dijo Voldemort, agachándose un poco, pero sin dejar de presentar a Harry su cara de serpiente—. Vamos, hay que comportarse como caballeros... A Dumbledore le gustaría que hicieras gala de tus buenos modales.<strong> Inclínate ante la muerte, Harry</strong>. </em></span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1169592304">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1169592304" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15154637-kate" class="left imgcol" title="Kate ?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450402290p2/15154637.jpg" alt="Kate ?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1169592304?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15154637-kate" class="user" title="Kate ?">Kate ?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7979788-harry-potter-and-the-goblet-of-fire" title="Paperback 9781408810576" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/15154637-kate?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15154637-kate?shelf=2015-read" class="actionLinkLite">2015-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1169592304">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11365952985244600904"><strong>BLOG POST REVIEW:</strong><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://thebookgram.wordpress.com/2015/08/16/harry-potter-and-the-goblet-of-fire-review/" target="_blank">https://thebookgram.wordpress.com/201...</a><br /><br /><em>Actual Rating: 4.5/5 stars</em><br />Ah, J.K. Rowling truly is a genius! The way this book is moulded together is a true art and masterpiece. It continues to baffle me how one could come up with such an incredible story like this, simply from their own mind.<br /><br />In this novel, we begin to see the start of Ron and Hermione’s future relationship, and it was so cute to read about Ron’s obvious jealousy.<br /><br />This book really set up the eerie tone for the next book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11365952985244600904"><strong>BLOG POST REVIEW:</strong><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://thebookgram.wordpress.com/2015/08/16/harry-potter-and-the-goblet-of-fire-review/" target="_blank">https://thebookgram.wordpress.com/201...</a><br /><br /><em>Actual Rating: 4.5/5 stars</em><br />Ah, J.K. Rowling truly is a genius! The way this book is moulded together is a true art and masterpiece. It continues to baffle me how one could come up with such an incredible story like this, simply from their own mind.<br /><br />In this novel, we begin to see the start of Ron and Hermione’s future relationship, and it was so cute to read about Ron’s obvious jealousy.<br /><br />This book really set up the eerie tone for the next books, and I can’t wait to see how dark the story ends up going, as I know it definitely gets a-lot darker in terms of the movies.<br /><br />I loved Dumbledore and Sirius in this, and Hermione’s bad-assery really started to kick off towards the end! I can’t wait to see how that progresses. The words Dumbledore says just shows how wise he is, and I love it!<br /><br />J.K. Rowling’s use of the Dementors is an incredible link to what they’re supposed to represent, which is depression. I’ll share with you a line that made me appreciate Ms. Rowling’s brain on this even more than I previously did:<br /><br />“Most go mad in there, and plenty stop eating in the end. They lose the will to live. You could always tell when a death was coming, because the Dementors could sense it, they got excited.”<br /><br />There certainly are some incredible quotes and passages throughout this novel, and I bow down to you, J.K. Rowling. I’m so excited to continue to read how Harry and his friends grow and mature, as the tone of the book does also.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11365952985244600904">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_38425392">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38425392" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu" class="left imgcol" title="Jason Koivu"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1440701539p2/1742824.jpg" alt="Jason Koivu" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38425392?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 21, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu" class="user" title="Jason Koivu">Jason Koivu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Paperback 9780439139601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38425392">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14145358019884920093">If the "shit got real" in the last book, well, in this fourth book shit got unreal.<br /><br /><em>Goblet of Fire</em> took the series forward and yet in tone it felt like a regression to the first two books. Certainly it is darker and slightly more mature in subject matter. However, there's a lingering "freshman" feel which I blame on the inclusion of the Tri Wizard Tournament. It seemed out of place at this point in the story. <br /><br />I have no problem with the idea that the wizarding establishment didn't believe (or want</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14145358019884920093">If the "shit got real" in the last book, well, in this fourth book shit got unreal.<br /><br /><em>Goblet of Fire</em> took the series forward and yet in tone it felt like a regression to the first two books. Certainly it is darker and slightly more mature in subject matter. However, there's a lingering "freshman" feel which I blame on the inclusion of the Tri Wizard Tournament. It seemed out of place at this point in the story. <br /><br />I have no problem with the idea that the wizarding establishment didn't believe (or want to believe) that Voldemort was back and ergo they would naturally carry on with their lives, as would the students, so the big sporting event is not precisely my issue. It's the amount of time spent on the event I'm taking to task. As readers, we know the ultimate evil has come again, so it's hard to suspend our dread and enjoy the fun and games of the tournament, or at least it was hard for me. <br /><br />Others I've spoke to don't seem to mind the "fun and games" aspect of this book. However, to me it seemed like Rowling hadn't given the storyline maturation its due. Was this a lack of skill on her part? Mishandling of story pacing is just as important as plot, realistic characters, appropriate dialogue and knowing how to put one word after another in the correct order. <br /><br />Perhaps the "let them eat cake" atmosphere of tragedy veiled is <em>just</em> what was called for. Time and again, history proves this scenario holds true for some. I wasn't buying it though.<br /><br /><strong>Rating: 3.5</strong> - <em>Goblet...</em> gets perhaps a higher rating from me than you'd think after reading that complainypants review, but the fact is the book is still entertaining, and at this point I was so very wrapped up in the series that Rowling could've taken a dump, published it and I would've given it at least two stars. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14145358019884920093">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49538742" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/885654-liza-martin" class="left imgcol" title="Liza Martin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1206986990p2/885654.jpg" alt="Liza Martin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/49538742?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/885654-liza-martin" class="user" title="Liza Martin">Liza Martin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Paperback 9780439139601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer49538742">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1121244331378824350">So after suffering through the first three books of this series, I vowed never to carry on and finish it. That is, until I was at a party and two of my friends gave the Harry Potter saga such a ringing endorsement that I was convinced I was missing out. I picked up the fourth book and was determined to read it, to reconsider my stance on the series.<br /><br />I quickly got through 200 pages, but it was then that I came to the same crisis I always do when reading a Harry Potter book: Do I really want to go</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1121244331378824350">So after suffering through the first three books of this series, I vowed never to carry on and finish it. That is, until I was at a party and two of my friends gave the Harry Potter saga such a ringing endorsement that I was convinced I was missing out. I picked up the fourth book and was determined to read it, to reconsider my stance on the series.<br /><br />I quickly got through 200 pages, but it was then that I came to the same crisis I always do when reading a Harry Potter book: Do I really want to go on?<br /><br />And as always, the answer was no. So in keeping with my MO that "Life is too short to read books you're not interested in," I put it down and have no regrets.<br /><br />Sorry, Harry and the gang, I just have no interest in you or your adventures. I guess I never really "got" this phenomenon, and that's OK with me. There are better books out there.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1121244331378824350">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_262535509">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262535509" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4901961-jay-kristoff" class="left imgcol" title="Jay Kristoff"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296449592p2/4901961.jpg" alt="Jay Kristoff" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/262535509?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4901961-jay-kristoff" class="user" title="Jay Kristoff">Jay Kristoff</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Paperback 9780439139601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer262535509">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer826844290922061686">This was the book that broke me from the HP series. My bride insists they got better, but she also married me, so her taste is... suspect.<br /><br />I loved Prisoner of Azkaban. Great struggle, clever time-travel story (very hard to do) and our first real glimpses of the dark places where this series would head. I liked that shift, I really did. So what broke me?<br /><br />Firstly, the plot holes. Well, more accurately, one plot hole, but it was a frackin' doozy. You know the opening scene in Star Wars where the came</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText826844290922061686">This was the book that broke me from the HP series. My bride insists they got better, but she also married me, so her taste is... suspect.<br /><br />I loved Prisoner of Azkaban. Great struggle, clever time-travel story (very hard to do) and our first real glimpses of the dark places where this series would head. I liked that shift, I really did. So what broke me?<br /><br />Firstly, the plot holes. Well, more accurately, one plot hole, but it was a frackin' doozy. You know the opening scene in Star Wars where the camera is beneath the belly of the Star Destroyer and the shot just goes on and on for about ten frackin' minutes and you can practically hear George Lucas yelling "That's right, Star Destroyers are REALLY BIG, bitches!"? Well, this was a Star Destroyer sized plot hole. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Rowling goes to some length spelling out that portkeys can be anything. A cup. A book. A fluffy bunny. She also establishes that you can't teleport in and out of Hogwarts, because it's warded. Fair enough. BUT, Harry and his chums have often left the grounds of HG's, to go and drink 'butterbeer' or buy living chocolate frogs or snog in alleyways or whatever. The precedent has been set that they can and do leave the school grounds. FFS, Harry lived outside of Hogwarts for YEARS (and yeah Uncle Owen and Aunt Beru's [or whatever] place was magicked so folks couldn't find him, but how did he get back and forth to it, eh? A TRAIN.)<br /><br />SO, you are an evil overlord trying to take over the world. You need Harry's blood to get your body back. You have an agent WITHIN Hogwarts, despite all these magical defenses, disguised as a teacher that Harry implicitly trusts.<br /><br />Do you:<br /><br />a) Set in place an elaborate ruse, framed around this enormous tri-wizard tournament, which (presumably) is under scrutiny by the most powerful wizards in the world and the ministry of magic, in which you manipulate events so that Harry not only enters the tournament (despite rules that expressly say that he's not old enough) but wins it, touches the tri-wizard cup, which, despite all these defenses and wizard-y scrutiny and security, you've managed to turn into a frackin' portkey (yes, you're that good) so that he gets teleported away from the tourney grounds into your evil clutches and hey, you bleed that bitch.<br /><br />b) Have your agent (who Harry implicitly trusts) say "hey Potter, what's say we head down to the pub for a mug of butterbeer and I'll tell you some stuff about your dad/mum/long lost twin?" use all your evil-wizardyness to change a mug of butterbeer into a portkey, and save everyone around 400 pages of this book.<br /><br />Sorry, but I didn't buy it. I've read many fan arguments explaining why the tri-wizard tournament and everything around it wasn't window-dressing on an overly complicated plan, the fruits of which could have very easily been borne by a far less convoluted and complex Evil Scheme(tm) which, granted, probably wouldn't have made a very interesting book, but YOUR WAREZ, I AM NOT BUYING THEM. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But second, and more importantly, it was in GoF that I realized that Harry was going to win. That he was just awesome, and no matter what rules were set in place (you're too young to enter the tournament/you're ten years old, why on earth would we put you in the CLUTCH position on our Quidditch team/you wear glasses, the ladiez don't dig dudes in glasses) he would triumph. Rowling LOVED Harry. She loved all the Harry gang. Too much. And it became painfully obvious that these kids were going to win, without a single fatality/crippling sacrifice/crushing loss. That in the end, Voldemort would be beaten, and Harry would marry Ginny, and Ron would marry Hermione and everyone would live happily ever after and make lots of adorable wizard babies.<br /><br />This was the book Harry ceased being a character and became a caricature. A SUPERHERO. Superheros bore me. I want torment. I want LOSS. I want my heroes to pay a TANGIBLE and TERRIBLE price for their victories. And no, killing tertiary characters doesn't count. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Digory? The Weasley twin? Even Dumbledore (yeah I know he dies, I got spoiled) is disposable.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I need to believe my heroes could fail. I know they probably won't. I know the good guys will eventually win. But I need to be afraid for them. I need to be scanning the faces of the MAIN characters and wondering "which one of you will be dead/emotionally crippled/hideously disfigured before the final act is over?" And I never believed for a second that Rowling would harm a hair on their heady-head-heads.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[And, turns out, she didn't. :P <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(shrugs)<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="826844290922061686">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class="brown_comment" id="comment_139016292">
  <div class="xhr_comment_photo">
    	<a href="/user/show/20610000-kaitlin-reif" alt="Kaitlin Reif"><img alt="20610000" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408155332p1/20610000.jpg" /></a>
  </div>
  <div class="xhr_comment_body">
    <a href="/user/show/20610000-kaitlin-reif" style="font-weight:bold">Kaitlin Reif</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer17093050963274523120">I think your viewing of the tournament as an overly elaborate plan to get what is essentially three drops of Harry’s blood is totally fair based on yo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17093050963274523120">I think your viewing of the tournament as an overly elaborate plan to get what is essentially three drops of Harry’s blood is totally fair based on your assessment of Voldemort as “ruthless, methodical, and calculating.” All due respect, but the problem with your plot hole rant is that your assessment of V’s character is not quite right. Or at least, not fully developed. There are many instances of Voldemort being your standard malevolent Dark Lord, killing indiscriminately and efficiently. However, where Harry is concerned, he is indeed reckless, even increasingly negligent as he tries to crush the optimism linked to “the boy who lived.” He doesn’t just want to use him and kill him, he wants to humiliate and destroy him for the entire world to see. Which is why he-- in his efforts to reinstate his good Bad Name among the wizarding community-- chooses scenarios in which he can publicly belittle Harry’s “savior” role, by destroying him in a grand and demoralizing way. How else do you get your street cred back, when the baby who did you in still lives… and everyone knows it?<br /><br />What you’re failing to consider with the tournament hoopla, is that Voldemort fully believed that Mad-Eye would not only ensure that Harry successfully made it to the cup first (how hard is it to bewitch a few teens in a super secret maze when you’re a powerful dark wizard? He had a year to plan it out!), but that he would also be successful in his return to bodily form and successful in killing Harry that night, in front of his troupe of unfaithful servants. If you imagine that V successfully murdered Harry in the graveyard, you can play out an alternate ending in which Voldemort sends Harry’s corpse back to the Hogwarts stadium with a chilling smoke monster message, “I’m back. And don’t think this one will save you this time.” It would be a dispiriting inversion of Harry’s Tri-Wizard victory: “Here’s your champion, dead at your feet.” Voldemort would be so fully gratified in that moment, destroying the one symbol of hope that the ministry had clung to over the last 13 years. An elaborate plan, perhaps, but to an all-powerful dark wizard, it guaranteed the right amount of sensational showmanship in the end. That was worth it to Voldemort. Once you understand V’s character in regards to Harry, it’s not difficult to buy into his strategy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17093050963274523120">...more</a>

    <br />

    <span class="xhrCommentFooter greyText">
      21 de Ago 20:20

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2OKftr+jDppRIngX+Ge+gt59rDu1IIxHxSdIxHz2ey69NqBlTXEaYN36DKyGBlgwl4pvIvz9y+2vLk1WsGONaw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gD64EP0fSbMJeVj9HDdbKYKfaKC2SnPuGrilvnX9x5bl6ofDD81dSYWhLEZiVr2by2iruf+XNERwsaAsuWgx0w==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling">About J.K. Rowling</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling"><img alt="1077326" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1415945171p2/1077326.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14280406006329318658">See also: <a title="Robert Galbraith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <strong>J.K. Rowling</strong>, pronounced like <em>rolling</em>, her name when her first <em>Harry Potter</em> book was published was simply <strong>Joanne Rowling</strong>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she ch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14280406006329318658">See also: <a title="Robert Galbraith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <strong>J.K. Rowling</strong>, pronounced like <em>rolling</em>, her name when her first <em>Harry Potter</em> book was published was simply <strong>Joanne Rowling</strong>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she chose <strong>K</strong> as the second initial of her pen name, from her paternal grandmother Kathleen Ada Bulgen Rowling. She calls herself <strong>Jo</strong> and has said, "No one ever called me 'Joanne' when I was young, unless they were angry." Following her marriage, she has sometimes used the name <strong>Joanne Murray</strong> when conducting personal business. During the Leveson Inquiry she gave evidence under the name of <strong>Joanne Kathleen Rowling</strong>. In a 2012 interview, Rowling noted that she no longer cared that people pronounced her name incorrectly.<br /><br />Rowling was born to Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, and Anne Rowling (née Volant), on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) northeast of Bristol. Her mother Anne was half-French and half-Scottish. Her parents first met on a train departing from King's Cross Station bound for Arbroath in 1964. They married on 14 March 1965. Her mother's maternal grandfather, Dugald Campbell, was born in Lamlash on the Isle of Arran. Her mother's paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was awarded the Croix de Guerre for exceptional bravery in defending the village of Courcelles-le-Comte during the First World War.<br /><br />Rowling's sister Dianne was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old. The family moved to the nearby village Winterbourne when Rowling was four. She attended St Michael's Primary School, a school founded by abolitionist William Wilberforce and education reformer Hannah More. Her headmaster at St Michael's, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the <em>Harry Potter</em> headmaster Albus Dumbledore.<br /><br />As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories, which she would usually then read to her sister. She recalls that: "I can still remember me telling her a story in which she fell down a rabbit hole and was fed strawberries by the rabbit family inside it. Certainly the first story I ever wrote down (when I was five or six) was about a rabbit called Rabbit. He got the measles and was visited by his friends, including a giant bee called Miss Bee." At the age of nine, Rowling moved to Church Cottage in the Gloucestershire village of Tutshill, close to Chepstow, Wales. When she was a young teenager, her great aunt, who Rowling said "taught classics and approved of a thirst for knowledge, even of a questionable kind," gave her a very old copy of Jessica Mitford's autobiography, <em>Hons and Rebels</em>. Mitford became Rowling's heroine, and Rowling subsequently read all of her books.<br /><br />Rowling has said of her teenage years, in an interview with The New Yorker, "I wasn’t particularly happy. I think it’s a dreadful time of life." She had a difficult homelife; her mother was ill and she had a difficult relationship with her father (she is no longer on speaking terms with him). She attended secondary school at Wyedean School and College, where her mother had worked as a technician in the science department. Rowling said of her adolescence, "Hermione [a bookish, know-it-all <em>Harry Potter</em> character] is loosely based on me. She's a caricature of me when I was eleven, which I'm not particularly proud of." Steve Eddy, who taught Rowling English when she first arrived, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English." Sean Harris, her best friend in the Upper Sixth owned a turquoise Ford Anglia, which she says inspired the one in her books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14280406006329318658">...more</a>

    </div>
